#####################
### Modular model ### 
##################### 

### Construction ~ Temporal proximity + Link to t0 + Intention + Contingency + Speaker certainty | Grammatical person + animacy | Verb class


## The binary mixed effects models were run with both lme4 (glmer) and mclogit (mblogit) to corroborate results. 
## Regardless of the package used, if the full model (with both random variabels) is included, one receives a warning that the algorithms did not converge.
## This error means that one of the regressors (IVs) is perfectly predicting the outcome. It is common practice to run a penalised model in this context 
## but given that this problem only occurs when /both/ random variabels are added to the models indicates that this needs further investigation.
## It is likely that the error itself would be informative in a descriptive study. 


library(lme4)
library(languageR)
library(Hmisc)
# load complete data
df <- read.table(file.choose(), header=T, sep="\t", stringsAsFactors = T)
summary(df)


## Model with all nominal IVs
M_Nom = glmer(Cx ~ Link_to_t0.Coarse + Contingency.Coarse + Intention + Temporal_proximityA + Speaker_certaintyD + (1 | Verb_type1) + (1 |  Person_animacy.1), family = binomial("logit"), control = glmerControl(optimizer ="Nelder_Mead"), data = df)
summary(M_Nom)

## After backward selection, significant IVs only - Temporal_proximityA removed

M_Nom = glmer(Cx ~ Link_to_t0.Coarse + Contingency.Coarse + Intention + Speaker_certaintyD + (1 | Verb_type1) + (1 |  Person_animacy.1), family = binomial("logit"), control = glmerControl(optimizer ="Nelder_Mead"), data = df)
summary(M_Nom)

## If pvalues are missing, run library(languageR)
pvals.fnc(M_Nom, nsim=10000)

# VIFs
# To calculate the VIFs, run the scripts attached first
vif.mer(M_Nom)
max(vif.mer(M_Nom))

# Concordance
# This did not run under R 4.2.2, but runs under (at least) R3.6. 
# Author will solve problem and update file in future.
# Until then, calculate C with concordance command in the survival package, on a model fit with mclogit (see below)
somers2((probs = binomial()$linkinv(fitted(M_Nom))), as.numeric(df$Cx)-1)


library(mclogit)
library(survival)
M_Nom_b = mblogit(Cx ~ Link_to_t0.Coarse + Contingency.Coarse + Intention + Speaker_certaintyD, ~ 1 | Verb_type1 / Person_animacy.1, data = df)
summary(M_Nom_b)
concordance(M_Nom_b)


## Model with mixed nominal and ordinal IVs

## coming soon, but the same as above.
## interpreting ordinal predictors in the table of coefficients requires comment


## Note that the VIFS and C score ont heir own are not enough to evaluate the fit of a model. They were used in this study as a bare minimum since the aim was methodological not descriptive.



####################
### Family model ### 
####################


### Construction ~ Temporal proximity + Link to t0 + Intention + Contingency + Speaker certainty | Grammatical person + animacy | Verb class
## Full model with all nominal IVs

library(mclogit)
library(survival)


m = mblogit(Cx.Prs ~ Intention + Contingency.Coarse + Link_to_t0.Coarse + Temporal_proximityA + Speaker_certaintyD, ~ 1 | Verb_type1, data = df)

> my.lmer.nagelkerke(c("Cx ~ Link_to_t0.Coarse + Contingency.Coarse + Intention + Temporal_proximityA + Speaker_certaintyD", "(1 | Verb_type1)"), df)

  unused argument (family = "binomial")
> my.lmer.nagelkerke <- function(f, d) {
+  lmer.full= lmer(formula= as.formula(paste(f, collapse="+")), d, family="binomial")
+  logLik.lmer.full= as.numeric(logLik(lmer.full))
+  N.lmer.full= nrow(lmer.full@X)
+  cat(paste("Full mixed model: L=", logLik.lmer.full, ", N=", N.lmer.full, "\n", sep=""))
+ 
+  lmer.intercept= lmer(formula= as.formula(paste(unlist(strsplit(f[1], "~"))[1], paste("1", f[2], sep=" + "), sep="~ ")), data= d, family="binomial")
+  logLik.lmer.intercept= as.numeric(logLik(lmer.intercept))
+  N.lmer.intercept= nrow(lmer.intercept@X)
+  cat(paste("Intercept mixed model: L=", logLik.lmer.intercept, ", N=", N.lmer.intercept, "\n", sep=""))
+ 
+  lrm.full= lrm(formula= as.formula(f[1]), data= d)
+  logLik.lrm.intercept= as.numeric(deviance(lrm.full)[1] / - 2)
+  N.lrm.intercept= as.numeric(lrm.full$stats[1])
+  cat(paste("Intercept ordinary model: L=", logLik.lrm.intercept, ", N=", N.lrm.intercept, "\n", sep=""))
+ 
+  coxsnell.lmer= 1 - exp((logLik.lmer.intercept - logLik.lmer.full) * (2/N.lmer.full))
+  nagelkerke.lmer= coxsnell.lmer / (1 - exp(logLik.lmer.intercept * (2/N.lmer.full)))
+  cat(paste("Full model evaluated against mixed intercept model:\n\tCoxSnell R2: ", coxsnell.lmer, "\n\tNagelkerke R2: ", nagelkerke.lmer,"\n", sep=""))
+  coxsnell.lrm= 1 - exp((logLik.lrm.intercept - logLik.lmer.full) * (2/N.lmer.full))
+  nagelkerke.lrm= coxsnell.lrm / (1 - exp(logLik.lrm.intercept * (2/N.lmer.full)))
+  cat(paste("Full model evaluated against ordinary intercept model:\n\tCoxSnell R2: ", coxsnell.lrm, "\n\tNagelkerke R2: ", nagelkerke.lrm,"\n", sep=""))
+  coxsnell.lrm.2= 1 - exp((logLik.lrm.intercept - logLik.lmer.intercept) * (2/N.lmer.full))
+  nagelkerke.lrm.2= coxsnell.lrm.2 / (1 - exp(logLik.lrm.intercept * (2/N.lmer.full)))
+  cat(paste("Mixed intercept model evaluated against ordinary intercept model:\n\tCoxSnell R2: ", coxsnell.lrm.2, "\n\tNagelkerke R2: ", nagelkerke.lrm.2,"\n", sep=""))
+ }
> 
> ## Script for working out Vifs
> 
> vif.mer <- function (fit) {
+ ## adapted from rms::vif
+ v <- vcov(fit)
+ nam <- names(fixef(fit))
+ ## exclude intercepts
+ ns <- sum(1 * (nam == "Intercept" | nam == "(Intercept)"))
+ if (ns > 0) {
+ v <- v[-(1:ns), -(1:ns), drop = FALSE]
+ nam <- nam[-(1:ns)]
+ }
+ d <- diag(v)^0.5
+ v <- diag(solve(v/(d %o% d)))
+ names(v) <- nam
+ v
+ }
> 
> ## Script for working out Kappa estiamtes of collinearity
> 
> kappa.mer <- function (fit,
+ scale = TRUE, center = FALSE,
+ add.intercept = TRUE,
+ exact = FALSE) {
+ X <- fit@X
+ nam <- names(fixef(fit))
+ ## exclude intercepts
+ nrp <- sum(1 * (nam == "(Intercept)"))
+ if (nrp > 0) {
+ X <- X[, -(1:nrp), drop = FALSE]
+ nam <- nam[-(1:nrp)]
+ }
+ if (add.intercept) {
+ X <- cbind(rep(1), scale(X, scale = scale, center = center))
+ kappa(X, exact = exact)
+ } else {
+ kappa(scale(X, scale = scale, center = scale), exact = exact)
+ }
+ }
> 
> ## Script for working out Condition indexes and variance decomposition proportions
> 
> colldiag.mer <- function (fit,
+ scale = TRUE, center = FALSE,
+ add.intercept = TRUE){
+ ## adapted from perturb::colldiag, method in Belsley, Kuh, and
+ ## Welsch (1980).  look for a high condition index (> 30) with
+ ## more than one high variance propotion.  see ?colldiag for more
+ ## tips.
+ result <- NULL
+ if (center)
+ add.intercept <- FALSE
+ if (is.matrix(fit) || is.data.frame(fit)) {
+ X <- as.matrix(fit)
+ nms <- colnames(fit)
+ }
+ else if (class(fit) == "mer") {
+ nms <- names(fixef(fit))
+ X <- fit@X
+ if (any(grepl("(Intercept)", nms))) {
+ add.intercept <- FALSE
+ }
+ }
+ X <- X[!is.na(apply(X, 1, all)), ]
+ if (add.intercept) {
+ X <- cbind(1, X)
+ colnames(X)[1] <- "(Intercept)"
+ }
+ X <- scale(X, scale = scale, center = center)
+ svdX <- svd(X)
+ svdX$d
+ condindx <- max(svdX$d)/svdX$d
+ dim(condindx) <- c(length(condindx), 1)
+ Phi = svdX$v %*% diag(1/svdX$d)
+ Phi <- t(Phi^2)
+ pi <- prop.table(Phi, 2)
+ colnames(condindx) <- "cond.index"
+ if (!is.null(nms)) {
+ rownames(condindx) <- nms
+ colnames(pi) <- nms
+ rownames(pi) <- nms
+ } else {
+ rownames(condindx) <- 1:length(condindx)
+ colnames(pi) <- 1:ncol(pi)
+ rownames(pi) <- 1:nrow(pi)
+ }
+ result <- data.frame(cbind(condindx, pi))
+ zapsmall(result)
+ }
> 
> 
> ## correlation estimates of collinearity
> maxcorr.mer <- function (fit,
+ exclude.intercept = TRUE) {
+ so <- summary(fit)
+ corF <- so@vcov@factors$correlation
+ nam <- names(fixef(fit))
+ ## exclude intercepts
+ ns <- sum(1 * (nam == "Intercept" | nam == "(Intercept)"))
+ if (ns > 0 & exclude.intercept) {
+ corF <- corF[-(1:ns), -(1:ns), drop = FALSE]
+ nam <- nam[-(1:ns)]
+ }
+ corF[!lower.tri(corF)] <- 0
+ maxCor <- max(corF)
+ minCor <- min(corF)
+ if (abs(maxCor) > abs(minCor)) {
+ zapsmall(maxCor)
+ } else {
+ zapsmall(minCor)
+ }
+ }
>
